| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.skipCredentialsValidation">skip\_credentials\_validation</a></code> | <code>bool</code> | (Optional) Skip credentials validation via the STS API. |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.skipMetadataApiCheck">skip\_metadata\_api\_check</a></code> | <code>bool</code> | (Optional) Skip usage of EC2 Metadata API. |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.skipRegionValidation">skip\_region\_validation</a></code> | <code>bool</code> | (Optional) Skip validation of provided region name. |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.skipRequestingAccountId">skip\_requesting\_account\_id</a></code> | <code>bool</code> | (Optional) Whether to skip requesting the account ID. |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.skipS3Checksum">skip\_s3\_checksum</a></code> | <code>bool</code> | (Optional) Do not include checksum when uploading S3 Objects. |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.sseCustomerKey">sse\_customer\_key</a></code> | <code>str</code> | (Optional) The key to use for encrypting state with Server-Side Encryption with Customer-Provided Keys (SSE-C). |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.stsEndpoint">sts\_endpoint</a></code> | <code>str</code> | (Optional) Custom endpoint for the AWS Security Token Service (STS) API. |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.stsRegion">sts\_region</a></code> | <code>str</code> | (Optional) AWS region for STS. |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.token">token</a></code> | <code>str</code> | (Optional) Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) token. |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.useLegacyWorkflow">use\_legacy\_workflow</a></code> | <code>bool</code> | (Optional) Use the legacy authentication workflow, preferring environment variables over backend configuration. |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.usePathStyle">use\_path\_style</a></code> | <code>bool</code> | (Optional) Enable path-style S3 URLs (https://&lt; HOST >/&lt; BUCKET > instead of https://&lt; BUCKET >.&lt; HOST >). |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.workspaceKeyPrefix">workspace\_key\_prefix</a></code> | <code>str</code> | (Optional) Prefix applied to the state path inside the bucket. |

***

##### `scope`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="scope" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.scope"></a>

- *Type:* constructs.Construct

***

##### `bucket`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="bucket" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.bucket"></a>

- *Type:* str

Name of the S3 Bucket.

***

##### `key`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="key" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.key"></a>

- *Type:* str

Path to the state file inside the S3 Bucket.

When using a non-default workspace, the state path will be /workspace\_key\_prefix/workspace\_name/key

***

##### `access_key`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="access_key" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.accessKey"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) AWS access key.

If configured, must also configure secret\_key.
This can also be sourced from
the AWS\_ACCESS\_KEY\_ID environment variable,
AWS shared credentials file (e.g. ~/.aws/credentials),
or AWS shared configuration file (e.g. ~/.aws/config).

***

##### `acl`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="acl" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.acl"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Canned ACL to be applied to the state file.

***

##### `allowed_account_ids`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="allowed_account_ids" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.allowedAccountIds"></a>

- *Type:* typing.List\[str]

(Optional) List of allowed AWS account IDs to prevent potential destruction of a live environment.

Conflicts with forbidden\_account\_ids.

***

##### `assume_role`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="assume_role" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.assumeRole"></a>

- *Type:* <a href="#cdktn.S3BackendAssumeRoleConfig">S3BackendAssumeRoleConfig</a>

Assuming an IAM Role can be configured in two ways.

The preferred way is to use the argument assume\_role, the other, which is deprecated, is with arguments at the top level.

***

##### ~~`assume_role_policy`~~<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="assume_role_policy" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.assumeRolePolicy"></a>

- *Type:* typing.List\[str]

(Optional) Set of Amazon Resource Names (ARNs) of IAM Policies describing further restricting permissions for the IAM Role being assumed.

***

##### ~~`assume_role_tags`~~<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="assume_role_tags" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.assumeRoleTags"></a>

##### `custom_ca_bundle`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="custom_ca_bundle" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.customCaBundle"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) File containing custom root and intermediate certificates.

Can also be set using the AWS\_CA\_BUNDLE environment variable.
Setting ca\_bundle in the shared config file is not supported.

***

##### ~~`dynamodb_endpoint`~~<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="dynamodb_endpoint" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.dynamodbEndpoint"></a>

- *Deprecated:* Use endpoints.dynamodb instead

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Custom endpoint for the AWS DynamoDB API.

This can also be sourced from the AWS\_DYNAMODB\_ENDPOINT environment variable.

***

##### `dynamodb_table`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="dynamodb_table" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.dynamodbTable"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Name of DynamoDB Table to use for state locking and consistency.

The table must have a partition key named LockID with type of String.
If not configured, state locking will be disabled.

***

##### `ec2_metadata_service_endpoint`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="ec2_metadata_service_endpoint" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.ec2MetadataServiceEndpoint"></a>

- *Type:* str

Optional) Custom endpoint URL for the EC2 Instance Metadata Service (IMDS) API.

Can also be set with the AWS\_EC2\_METADATA\_SERVICE\_ENDPOINT environment variable.

***

##### `ec2_metadata_service_endpoint_mode`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="ec2_metadata_service_endpoint_mode" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.ec2MetadataServiceEndpointMode"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Mode to use in communicating with the metadata service.

Valid values are IPv4 and IPv6.
Can also be set with the AWS\_EC2\_METADATA\_SERVICE\_ENDPOINT\_MODE environment variable.

***

##### `encrypt`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="encrypt" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.encrypt"></a>

- *Type:* bool

(Optional) Enable server side encryption of the state file.

***

- *Deprecated:* Use endpoints.s3 instead

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Custom endpoint for the AWS S3 API.

This can also be sourced from the AWS\_S3\_ENDPOINT environment variable.

***

##### `endpoints`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="endpoints" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.endpoints"></a>

- *Type:* <a href="#cdktn.S3BackendEndpointConfig">S3BackendEndpointConfig</a>

(Optional) The endpoint configuration block.

***

##### ~~`external_id`~~<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="external_id" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.externalId"></a>

##### `forbidden_account_ids`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="forbidden_account_ids" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.forbiddenAccountIds"></a>

##### ~~`force_path_style`~~<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="force_path_style" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.forcePathStyle"></a>

- *Deprecated:* Use usePathStyle instead

- *Type:* bool

(Optional) Enable path-style S3 URLs (https://&lt; HOST >/&lt; BUCKET > instead of https://&lt; BUCKET >.&lt; HOST >).

***

##### `http_proxy`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="http_proxy" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.httpProxy"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) URL of a proxy to use for HTTP requests when accessing the AWS API.

Can also be set using the HTTP\_PROXY or http\_proxy environment variables.

***

##### `https_proxy`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="https_proxy" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.httpsProxy"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) URL of a proxy to use for HTTPS requests when accessing the AWS API.

Can also be set using the HTTPS\_PROXY or https\_proxy environment variables.

***

##### ~~`iam_endpoint`~~<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="iam_endpoint" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.iamEndpoint"></a>

- *Deprecated:* Use endpoints.iam instead

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Custom endpoint for the AWS Identity and Access Management (IAM) API.

This can also be sourced from the AWS\_IAM\_ENDPOINT environment variable.

***

##### `insecure`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="insecure" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.insecure"></a>

- *Type:* bool

Optional) Whether to explicitly allow the backend to perform "insecure" SSL requests.

If omitted, the default value is false.

***

##### `kms_key_id`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="kms_key_id" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.kmsKeyId"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Amazon Resource Name (ARN) of a Key Management Service (KMS) Key to use for encrypting the state.

Note that if this value is specified,
Terraform will need kms:Encrypt, kms:Decrypt and kms:GenerateDataKey permissions on this KMS key.

***

##### `max_retries`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="max_retries" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.maxRetries"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Union\[int, float]

(Optional) The maximum number of times an AWS API request is retried on retryable failure.

Defaults to 5.

***

##### `no_proxy`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="no_proxy" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.noProxy"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Comma-separated list of hosts that should not use HTTP or HTTPS proxies.

Each value can be one of:

- A domain name
- An IP address
- A CIDR address
- An asterisk (\*), to indicate that no proxying should be performed Domain name and IP address values can also include a port number.
  Can also be set using the NO\_PROXY or no\_proxy environment variables.

***

##### `profile`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="profile" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.profile"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Name of AWS profile in AWS shared credentials file (e.g. ~/.aws/credentials) or AWS shared configuration file (e.g. ~/.aws/config) to use for credentials and/or configuration. This can also be sourced from the AWS\_PROFILE environment variable.

***

##### `region`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="region" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.region"></a>

- *Type:* str

AWS Region of the S3 Bucket and DynamoDB Table (if used).

This can also
be sourced from the AWS\_DEFAULT\_REGION and AWS\_REGION environment
variables.

***

##### `retry_mode`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="retry_mode" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.retryMode"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Specifies how retries are attempted.

Valid values are standard and adaptive.
Can also be configured using the AWS\_RETRY\_MODE environment variable or the shared config file parameter retry\_mode.

***

##### ~~`role_arn`~~<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="role_arn" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.roleArn"></a>

- *Deprecated:* Use assumeRole.roleArn instead.

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Amazon Resource Name (ARN) of the IAM Role to assume.

***

##### `secret_key`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="secret_key" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.secretKey"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) AWS secret access key.

If configured, must also configure access\_key.
This can also be sourced from
the AWS\_SECRET\_ACCESS\_KEY environment variable,
AWS shared credentials file (e.g. ~/.aws/credentials),
or AWS shared configuration file (e.g. ~/.aws/config)

***

##### ~~`session_name`~~<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="session_name" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.sessionName"></a>

- *Deprecated:* Use assumeRole.sessionName instead.

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Session name to use when assuming the role.

***

##### `shared_config_files`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="shared_config_files" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.sharedConfigFiles"></a>

- *Type:* typing.List\[str]

(Optional) List of paths to AWS shared configuration files.

Defaults to ~/.aws/config.

***

##### `shared_credentials_file`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="shared_credentials_file" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.sharedCredentialsFile"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Path to the AWS shared credentials file.

Defaults to ~/.aws/credentials.

***

##### `shared_credentials_files`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="shared_credentials_files" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.sharedCredentialsFiles"></a>

- *Type:* typing.List\[str]

(Optional) List of paths to AWS shared credentials files.

Defaults to ~/.aws/credentials.

***

##### `skip_credentials_validation`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="skip_credentials_validation" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.skipCredentialsValidation"></a>

- *Type:* bool

(Optional) Skip credentials validation via the STS API.

***

##### `skip_metadata_api_check`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="skip_metadata_api_check" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.skipMetadataApiCheck"></a>

- *Type:* bool

(Optional) Skip usage of EC2 Metadata API.

***

##### `skip_region_validation`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="skip_region_validation" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.skipRegionValidation"></a>

- *Type:* bool

(Optional) Skip validation of provided region name.

***

##### `skip_requesting_account_id`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="skip_requesting_account_id" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.skipRequestingAccountId"></a>

- *Type:* bool

(Optional) Whether to skip requesting the account ID.

Useful for AWS API implementations that do not have the IAM, STS API, or metadata API.

***

##### `skip_s3_checksum`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="skip_s3_checksum" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.skipS3Checksum"></a>

- *Type:* bool

(Optional) Do not include checksum when uploading S3 Objects.

Useful for some S3-Compatible APIs.

***

##### `sse_customer_key`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="sse_customer_key" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.sseCustomerKey"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) The key to use for encrypting state with Server-Side Encryption with Customer-Provided Keys (SSE-C).

This is the base64-encoded value of the key, which must decode to 256 bits.
This can also be sourced from the AWS\_SSE\_CUSTOMER\_KEY environment variable,
which is recommended due to the sensitivity of the value.
Setting it inside a terraform file will cause it to be persisted to disk in terraform.tfstate.

***

##### ~~`sts_endpoint`~~<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="sts_endpoint" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.stsEndpoint"></a>

- *Deprecated:* Use endpoints.sts instead

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Custom endpoint for the AWS Security Token Service (STS) API.

This can also be sourced from the AWS\_STS\_ENDPOINT environment variable.

***

##### `sts_region`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="sts_region" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.stsRegion"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) AWS region for STS.

If unset, AWS will use the same region for STS as other non-STS operations.

***

##### `token`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="token" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.token"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) token.

This can also be sourced from the AWS\_SESSION\_TOKEN environment variable.

***

##### `use_legacy_workflow`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="use_legacy_workflow" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.useLegacyWorkflow"></a>

- *Type:* bool

(Optional) Use the legacy authentication workflow, preferring environment variables over backend configuration.

Defaults to true.
This behavior does not align with the authentication flow of the AWS CLI or SDK's, and will be removed in the future.

***

##### `use_path_style`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="use_path_style" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.usePathStyle"></a>

- *Type:* bool

(Optional) Enable path-style S3 URLs (https://&lt; HOST >/&lt; BUCKET > instead of https://&lt; BUCKET >.&lt; HOST >).

***

##### `workspace_key_prefix`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="workspace_key_prefix" id="cdktn.S3Backend.Initializer.parameter.workspaceKeyPrefix"></a>

- *Type:* str

(Optional) Prefix applied to the state path inside the bucket.

This is only relevant when using a non-default workspace. Defaults to env:

***

##### `is_construct` <a name="is_construct" id="cdktn.S3Backend.isConstruct"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.S3Backend.is_construct(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

Checks if `x` is a construct.

Use this method instead of `instanceof` to properly detect `Construct`
instances, even when the construct library is symlinked.

Explanation: in JavaScript, multiple copies of the `constructs` library on
disk are seen as independent, completely different libraries. As a
consequence, the class `Construct` in each copy of the `constructs` library
is seen as a different class, and an instance of one class will not test as
`instanceof` the other class. `npm install` will not create installations
like this, but users may manually symlink construct libraries together or
use a monorepo tool: in those cases, multiple copies of the `constructs`
library can be accidentally installed, and `instanceof` will behave
unpredictably. It is safest to avoid using `instanceof`, and using
this type-testing method instead.

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.S3Backend.isConstruct.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

Any object.

***

##### `is_terraform_element` <a name="is_terraform_element" id="cdktn.S3Backend.isTerraformElement"></a>


##### ~~`is_construct`~~ <a name="is_construct" id="cdktn.SwiftBackend.isConstruct"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.SwiftBackend.is_construct(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

Checks if `x` is a construct.

Use this method instead of `instanceof` to properly detect `Construct`
instances, even when the construct library is symlinked.

Explanation: in JavaScript, multiple copies of the `constructs` library on
disk are seen as independent, completely different libraries. As a
consequence, the class `Construct` in each copy of the `constructs` library
is seen as a different class, and an instance of one class will not test as
`instanceof` the other class. `npm install` will not create installations
like this, but users may manually symlink construct libraries together or
use a monorepo tool: in those cases, multiple copies of the `constructs`
library can be accidentally installed, and `instanceof` will behave
unpredictably. It is safest to avoid using `instanceof`, and using
this type-testing method instead.

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.SwiftBackend.isConstruct.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

Any object.

***

##### ~~`is_terraform_element`~~ <a name="is_terraform_element" id="cdktn.SwiftBackend.isTerraformElement"></a>

```python

cdktn.SwiftBackend.is_terraform_element(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

use a monorepo tool: in those cases, multiple copies of the `constructs`
library can be accidentally installed, and `instanceof` will behave
unpredictably. It is safest to avoid using `instanceof`, and using
this type-testing method instead.

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.TerraformBackend.isConstruct.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

Any object.

***

#### Initializers <a name="Initializers" id="cdktn.TerraformDataSource.Initializer"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformDataSource(
  scope: Construct,
  id: str,
  connection: SSHProvisionerConnection | WinrmProvisionerConnection = None,
  count: typing.Union[int, float] | TerraformCount = None,
  depends_on: typing.List[ITerraformDependable] = None,
  for_each: ITerraformIterator = None,
  lifecycle: TerraformResourceLifecycle = None,
  provider: TerraformProvider = None,
  provisioners: typing.List[FileProvisioner | LocalExecProvisioner | RemoteExecProvisioner] = None,

)
```

***

##### `is_construct` <a name="is_construct" id="cdktn.TerraformDataSource.isConstruct"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformDataSource.is_construct(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

Checks if `x` is a construct.

Use this method instead of `instanceof` to properly detect `Construct`
instances, even when the construct library is symlinked.

Explanation: in JavaScript, multiple copies of the `constructs` library on
disk are seen as independent, completely different libraries. As a
consequence, the class `Construct` in each copy of the `constructs` library
is seen as a different class, and an instance of one class will not test as
`instanceof` the other class. `npm install` will not create installations
like this, but users may manually symlink construct libraries together or
use a monorepo tool: in those cases, multiple copies of the `constructs`
library can be accidentally installed, and `instanceof` will behave
unpredictably. It is safest to avoid using `instanceof`, and using
this type-testing method instead.

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.TerraformDataSource.isConstruct.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

Any object.

***

##### `is_terraform_element` <a name="is_terraform_element" id="cdktn.TerraformDataSource.isTerraformElement"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformDataSource.is_terraform_element(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

***

##### `is_construct` <a name="is_construct" id="cdktn.TerraformElement.isConstruct"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformElement.is_construct(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

Checks if `x` is a construct.

Use this method instead of `instanceof` to properly detect `Construct`
instances, even when the construct library is symlinked.

Explanation: in JavaScript, multiple copies of the `constructs` library on
disk are seen as independent, completely different libraries. As a
consequence, the class `Construct` in each copy of the `constructs` library
is seen as a different class, and an instance of one class will not test as
`instanceof` the other class. `npm install` will not create installations
like this, but users may manually symlink construct libraries together or
use a monorepo tool: in those cases, multiple copies of the `constructs`
library can be accidentally installed, and `instanceof` will behave
unpredictably. It is safest to avoid using `instanceof`, and using
this type-testing method instead.

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.TerraformElement.isConstruct.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

Any object.

***

##### `is_terraform_element` <a name="is_terraform_element" id="cdktn.TerraformElement.isTerraformElement"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformElement.is_terraform_element(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.TerraformElement.isTerraformElement.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

***

| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformElement.property.cdktfStack">cdktf\_stack</a></code> | <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformStack">TerraformStack</a></code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformElement.property.fqn">fqn</a></code> | <code>str</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformElement.property.friendlyUniqueId">friendly\_unique\_id</a></code> | <code>str</code> | *No description.* |

```python

cdktn.TerraformHclModule.is_construct(
  x: typing.Any
```

##### `is_construct` <a name="is_construct" id="cdktn.TerraformLocal.isConstruct"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformLocal.is_construct(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

Checks if `x` is a construct.

Use this method instead of `instanceof` to properly detect `Construct`
instances, even when the construct library is symlinked.

Explanation: in JavaScript, multiple copies of the `constructs` library on
disk are seen as independent, completely different libraries. As a
consequence, the class `Construct` in each copy of the `constructs` library
is seen as a different class, and an instance of one class will not test as
`instanceof` the other class. `npm install` will not create installations
like this, but users may manually symlink construct libraries together or
use a monorepo tool: in those cases, multiple copies of the `constructs`
library can be accidentally installed, and `instanceof` will behave
unpredictably. It is safest to avoid using `instanceof`, and using
this type-testing method instead.

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.TerraformLocal.isConstruct.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

Any object.

***

##### `is_terraform_element` <a name="is_terraform_element" id="cdktn.TerraformLocal.isTerraformElement"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformLocal.is_terraform_element(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.TerraformLocal.isTerraformElement.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

***

### TerraformModule <a name="TerraformModule" id="cdktn.TerraformModule"></a>

- *Implements:* <a href="#cdktn.ITerraformDependable">ITerraformDependable</a>

TerraformModule can be used to reference a local terraform module or a module from the Terraform Registry.

It should be used if you can not use generated bindings for the module as you would get by adding the module
to your cdktf.json files "terraformModules" array and running cdktn get.

This class is not creating a Terraform module to be used outside of CDKTN.
If you want to bundle certain resources together like you would do with a Terraform module,
you should use Constructs instead, see http://cdk.tf/constructs for more details.

#### Initializers <a name="Initializers" id="cdktn.TerraformModule.Initializer"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformModule(
  scope: Construct,
  id: str,
  depends_on: typing.List[ITerraformDependable] = None,
  for_each: ITerraformIterator = None,
  providers: typing.List[TerraformProvider | TerraformModuleProvider] = None,
  skip_asset_creation_from_local_modules: bool = None,
  source: str,
  version: str = None
)
```

| **Name** | **Type** | **Description** |
| --- | --- | --- |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformModule.Initializer.parameter.scope">scope</a></code> | <code>constructs.Construct</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformModule.Initializer.parameter.id">id</a></code> | <code>str</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformModule.Initializer.parameter.dependsOn">depends\_on</a></code> | <code>typing.List\[<a href="#cdktn.ITerraformDependable">ITerraformDependable</a>]</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformModule.Initializer.parameter.forEach">for\_each</a></code> | <code><a href="#cdktn.ITerraformIterator">ITerraformIterator</a></code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformModule.Initializer.parameter.providers">providers</a></code> | <code>typing.List\[<a href="#cdktn.TerraformProvider">TerraformProvider</a> &#124; <a href="#cdktn.TerraformModuleProvider">TerraformModuleProvider</a>]</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformModule.Initializer.parameter.skipAssetCreationFromLocalModules">skip\_asset\_creation\_from\_local\_modules</a></code> | <code>bool</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformModule.Initializer.parameter.source">source</a></code> | <code>str</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformModule.Initializer.parameter.version">version</a></code> | <code>str</code> | *No description.* |

***

##### `scope`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="scope" id="cdktn.TerraformModule.Initializer.parameter.scope"></a>

***

##### `id`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="id" id="cdktn.TerraformModule.Initializer.parameter.id"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformOutput(
```

##### `is_construct` <a name="is_construct" id="cdktn.TerraformOutput.isConstruct"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformOutput.is_construct(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

Checks if `x` is a construct.

Use this method instead of `instanceof` to properly detect `Construct`
instances, even when the construct library is symlinked.

Explanation: in JavaScript, multiple copies of the `constructs` library on
disk are seen as independent, completely different libraries. As a
consequence, the class `Construct` in each copy of the `constructs` library
is seen as a different class, and an instance of one class will not test as
`instanceof` the other class. `npm install` will not create installations
like this, but users may manually symlink construct libraries together or
use a monorepo tool: in those cases, multiple copies of the `constructs`
library can be accidentally installed, and `instanceof` will behave
unpredictably. It is safest to avoid using `instanceof`, and using
this type-testing method instead.

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.TerraformOutput.isConstruct.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

Any object.

***

##### `is_terraform_element` <a name="is_terraform_element" id="cdktn.TerraformOutput.isTerraformElement"></a>

```python
)
```

##### `is_construct` <a name="is_construct" id="cdktn.TerraformRemoteState.isConstruct"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformRemoteState.is_construct(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

Checks if `x` is a construct.

Use this method instead of `instanceof` to properly detect `Construct`
instances, even when the construct library is symlinked.

Explanation: in JavaScript, multiple copies of the `constructs` library on
disk are seen as independent, completely different libraries. As a
consequence, the class `Construct` in each copy of the `constructs` library
is seen as a different class, and an instance of one class will not test as
`instanceof` the other class. `npm install` will not create installations
like this, but users may manually symlink construct libraries together or
use a monorepo tool: in those cases, multiple copies of the `constructs`
library can be accidentally installed, and `instanceof` will behave
unpredictably. It is safest to avoid using `instanceof`, and using
this type-testing method instead.

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.TerraformRemoteState.isConstruct.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

Any object.

***

##### `is_terraform_element` <a name="is_terraform_element" id="cdktn.TerraformRemoteState.isTerraformElement"></a>

```python

cdktn.TerraformRemoteState.is_terraform_element(

)
```

- *Type:* str

The new logical ID to use for this stack element.

```python
) -> None
```

Move the resource corresponding to "id" to this resource.

Note that the resource being moved from must be marked as moved using it's instance function.

##### `is_construct` <a name="is_construct" id="cdktn.TerraformResource.isConstruct"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformResource.is_construct(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

Checks if `x` is a construct.

Use this method instead of `instanceof` to properly detect `Construct`
instances, even when the construct library is symlinked.

Explanation: in JavaScript, multiple copies of the `constructs` library on
disk are seen as independent, completely different libraries. As a
consequence, the class `Construct` in each copy of the `constructs` library
is seen as a different class, and an instance of one class will not test as
`instanceof` the other class. `npm install` will not create installations
like this, but users may manually symlink construct libraries together or
use a monorepo tool: in those cases, multiple copies of the `constructs`
library can be accidentally installed, and `instanceof` will behave
unpredictably. It is safest to avoid using `instanceof`, and using
this type-testing method instead.

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.TerraformResource.isConstruct.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

Any object.

***

##### `is_terraform_element` <a name="is_terraform_element" id="cdktn.TerraformResource.isTerraformElement"></a>

#### Static Functions <a name="Static Functions" id="Static Functions"></a>

| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformStack.isConstruct">is\_construct</a></code> | Checks if `x` is a construct. |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformStack.isStack">is\_stack</a></code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformStack.of">of</a></code> | *No description.* |

***

##### `is_construct` <a name="is_construct" id="cdktn.TerraformStack.isConstruct"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformStack.is_construct(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

Checks if `x` is a construct.

Use this method instead of `instanceof` to properly detect `Construct`
instances, even when the construct library is symlinked.

Explanation: in JavaScript, multiple copies of the `constructs` library on
disk are seen as independent, completely different libraries. As a
consequence, the class `Construct` in each copy of the `constructs` library
is seen as a different class, and an instance of one class will not test as
`instanceof` the other class. `npm install` will not create installations
like this, but users may manually symlink construct libraries together or
use a monorepo tool: in those cases, multiple copies of the `constructs`
library can be accidentally installed, and `instanceof` will behave
unpredictably. It is safest to avoid using `instanceof`, and using
this type-testing method instead.

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.TerraformStack.isConstruct.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

Any object.

***

##### `is_stack` <a name="is_stack" id="cdktn.TerraformStack.isStack"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformStack.is_stack(
  x: typing.Any
)
```

###### `x`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="x" id="cdktn.TerraformStack.isStack.parameter.x"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

***

### TerraformVariable <a name="TerraformVariable" id="cdktn.TerraformVariable"></a>

- *Implements:* <a href="#cdktn.ITerraformAddressable">ITerraformAddressable</a>

#### Initializers <a name="Initializers" id="cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer"></a>

```python
import cdktn

cdktn.TerraformVariable(
  scope: Construct,
  id: str,
  default: typing.Any = None,
  description: str = None,
  nullable: bool = None,
  sensitive: bool = None,
  type: str = None,
  validation: typing.List[TerraformVariableValidationConfig] = None
)
```

| **Name** | **Type** | **Description** |
| --- | --- | --- |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.scope">scope</a></code> | <code>constructs.Construct</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.id">id</a></code> | <code>str</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.default">default</a></code> | <code>typing.Any</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.description">description</a></code> | <code>str</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.nullable">nullable</a></code> | <code>bool</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.sensitive">sensitive</a></code> | <code>bool</code> | *No description.* |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.type">type</a></code> | <code>str</code> | The type argument in a variable block allows you to restrict the type of value that will be accepted as the value for a variable. |
| <code><a href="#cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.validation">validation</a></code> | <code>typing.List\[<a href="#cdktn.TerraformVariableValidationConfig">TerraformVariableValidationConfig</a>]</code> | Specify arbitrary custom validation rules for a particular variable using a validation block nested within the corresponding variable block. |

***

##### `scope`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="scope" id="cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.scope"></a>

***

##### `id`<sup>Required</sup> <a name="id" id="cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.id"></a>

- *Type:* str

***

##### `default`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="default" id="cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.default"></a>

- *Type:* typing.Any

***

##### `description`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="description" id="cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.description"></a>

- *Type:* str

***

##### `nullable`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="nullable" id="cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.nullable"></a>

- *Type:* bool

***

##### `sensitive`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="sensitive" id="cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.sensitive"></a>

- *Type:* bool

***

##### `type`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="type" id="cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.type"></a>

- *Type:* str

The type argument in a variable block allows you to restrict the type of value that will be accepted as the value for a variable.

If no type constraint is set then a value of any type is accepted.

While type constraints are optional, we recommend specifying them; they serve as easy reminders for users of the module, and allow Terraform to return a helpful error message if the wrong type is used.

Type constraints are created from a mixture of type keywords and type constructors. The supported type keywords are:

- string
- number
- bool

The type constructors allow you to specify complex types such as collections:

- list(&lt; TYPE >)
- set(&lt; TYPE >)
- map(&lt; TYPE >)
- object(\{&lt; ATTR NAME > = &lt; TYPE >, ... })
- tuple(\[&lt; TYPE >, ...])

The keyword any may be used to indicate that any type is acceptable. For more information on the meaning and behavior of these different types, as well as detailed information about automatic conversion of complex types, refer to [Type Constraints](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/expressions/type-constraints).

If both the type and default arguments are specified, the given default value must be convertible to the specified type.

***

##### `validation`<sup>Optional</sup> <a name="validation" id="cdktn.TerraformVariable.Initializer.parameter.validation"></a>

- *Type:* typing.List\[<a href="#cdktn.TerraformVariableValidationConfig">TerraformVariableValidationConfig</a>]

Specify arbitrary custom validation rules for a particular variable using a validation block nested within the corresponding variable block.

***
